(&#8220;Paragon&#8221;) (OTC: PGNPQ) today reported a </font><font style="font-

family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">&#32;</font><font style="font-

family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">&#32;per diluted share, as compared to 
</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">second 
quarter</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-
size:10pt;">&#32;</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-
size:10pt;">2015</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-
size:10pt;">&#32;net income of </font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-
size:10pt;">$47.3 million</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-
size:10pt;">, or </font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-
size:10pt;">$0.51</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-
size:10pt;">&#32;per diluted share. </font></div><div style="line-
height:120%;text-align:justify;padding-left:72px;text-indent:-24px;font-
size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-
size:10pt;"><br></font></div><div style="line-height:120%;text-
align:justify;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-
size:10pt;">Results for the </font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-
size:10pt;">second</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-
size:10pt;">&#32;quarter of </font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-
size:10pt;">2015</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-
size:10pt;">&#32;included a </font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-
size:10pt;">$4.1 million</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-
size:10pt;">, or $0.04 per diluted share, loss on the sale of an asset and 
a&#160;$1.7 million, or&#160;$0.02&#160;per diluted share, non-cash
 impairment charge related to assets which the company previously announced it 
had decided to retire from service. Excluding these charges, Paragon&#8217;s 
adjusted net income for the </font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-
size:10pt;">second</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-
size:10pt;">&#32;quarter of 2015 was </font><font style="font-
family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">$53.1 million</font><font style="font-
family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">, or </font><font style="font-
family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">$0.57</font><font style="font-
family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">&#32;per diluted share (for a reconciliation to 
net income for all &#8220;adjusted&#8221; metrics, see the Reconciliation of 
GAAP to Non-GAAP Financial Measures Table).</font></div><div style="line-
height:120%;text-align:justify;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-
family:inherit;font-size:10pt;"><br></font></div><div style="line-
height:120%;text-align:justify;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-
family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">Adjusted EBITDA is defined as net income (loss) 
before taxes, plus interest expense, depreciation, losses on impairments, 
foreign currency losses, and reorganization items, less gains on the sale of 
assets, interest income, and foreign currency gains.  For the </font><font 
style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">second</font><font style="font-
family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">&#32;quarter of 2016, adjusted EBITDA was 
</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">$66.0
million</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">, compared to 
</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">$115.4 
million</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">&#32;in the 
first quarter of 2016. </font></div><div style="line-height:120%;font-
size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-
size:10pt;"><br></font></div><div style="line-height:120%;text-
align:justify;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-
size:10pt;">&#8220;Despite the ongoing challenges in the offshore drilling 
industry, Paragon&#8217;s second quarter results reflect our continued focus on 
controlling costs and maintaining liquidity,&#8221; said Randall D. Stilley, 
President and Chief Executive Officer. &#8220;Utilization of the fleet declined 
and we responded quickly by stacking idle assets and lowering our contract 
drilling services costs by 19 percent compared to the first quarter of 2016.  We
also kept a tight control over capital expenditures and increased our cash 
balance to approximately $890 million, outperforming our 
expectations.&#8221;</font></div><div style="line-height:120%;text-
align:justify;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-
size:10pt;"><br></font></div><div style="line-height:120%;text-
align:justify;font-size:12pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-
size:10pt;">Total revenues for the </font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-
size:10pt;">second quarter</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-
size:10pt;">&#32;of </font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-
size:10pt;">2016</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-
size:10pt;">&#32;were </font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-
size:10pt;">$184.9 million</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-
size:10pt;">&#32;compared to </font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-
size:10pt;">$265.1 million</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-
size:10pt;">&#32;in the </font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-
size:10pt;">first</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-
size:10pt;">&#32;quarter of </font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-
size:10pt;">2016</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">. 
Paragon reported that utilization for its marketed rig fleet, which excludes 
available days related to rigs that were stacked and not marketed during the 
quarter, declined to </font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-
size:10pt;">38</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-
size:10pt;">&#32;percent for the </font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-
size:10pt;">second quarter</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-
size:10pt;">&#32;of 2016 compared to </font><font style="font-
family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">53</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-
size:10pt;">&#32;percent for the first quarter of 2016. Average daily revenues 
remained relatively flat in the </font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-
size:10pt;">second quarter</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-
size:10pt;">&#32;of </font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-
size:10pt;">2016</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">&#32;to
</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">$135,000</font><font 
style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">&#32;per rig compared to the 
previous quarter average of </font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-
size:10pt;">$135,000</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-
size:10pt;">&#32;per rig. Contract drilling services costs declined 19 percent 
in the </font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">second 
quarter</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">&#32;of 2016 to 
</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">$91.6 
million</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">&#32;compared to
</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">$112.7 
million</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">&#32;in the 
</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">first</font><font 
style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">&#32;quarter of </font><font 
style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">2016</font><font style="font-
family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">.</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-
size:12pt;">&#32;</font></div><div style="line-height:120%;text-
align:justify;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-
size:10pt;"><br></font></div><div style="line-height:120%;text-
align:justify;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-
size:10pt;">General and administrative (&#8220;G&amp;A&#8221;) costs for the
</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">second</font><font 
style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">&#32;quarter of 2016 totaled 
</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">$9.8 
million</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">&#32;compared to
</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">$12.2 
million</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">&#32;for the 
first quarter of 2016.  Reorganization costs totaled </font><font style="font-
family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">$17.5 million</font><font style="font-
family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">&#32;in the </font><font style="font-
family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">second</font><font style="font-
family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">&#32;quarter of 2016 compared to </font><font 
style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">$21.8 million</font><font 
style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">&#32;in the first quarter of 2016. 
</font></div><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:justify;font-
size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-
size:10pt;"><br></font></div><div style="line-height:120%;text-
align:justify;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-
size:10pt;">Net cash from operating activities was $101.8 million in the 
</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">second 
quarter</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">&#32;of 
</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">2016</font><font 
style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">&#32;as compared to $106.2 million 
for the </font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-
size:10pt;">first</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-
size:10pt;">&#32;quarter of </font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-
size:10pt;">2016</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">.  Cash
used for capital expenditures in the </font><font style="font-
family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">second quarter</font><font style="font-
family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">&#32;of 2016 totaled $12.0 million.  At 
</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">June&#160;30, 
2016</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">, liquidity, 
defined as cash and cash equivalents, totaled </font><font style="font-
family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">$889.1 million</font><font style="font-
family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">. </font></div><div><br></div><div style="text-

weight:bold;">Operating Highlights</font></div><div style="line-

style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">Paragon&#8217;s total contract 
backlog at </font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-
size:10pt;">June&#160;30, 2016</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-
size:10pt;">&#32;was approximately </font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-
size:10pt;">$472 million</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-
size:10pt;">&#32;compared to $806 million at </font><font style="font-
family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">March 31, 2016</font><font style="font-
family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">. Although Paragon continues to contest the 
approximately </font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">$143 
million</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">&#32;of backlog 
associated with what we believe to be an early release of the </font><font 
style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;font-style:italic;">Paragon
 DPDS3</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">&#32;by 
Paragon&#8217;s customer Petrobras, we have removed that amount from our June 
30, 2016 backlog total.   The March 31, 2016 backlog total included this 
disputed amount.</font></div><div style="line-height:120%;padding-
bottom:12px;text-align:justify;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-
family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">Utilization of Paragon&#8217;s marketed floating
rig fleet declined to </font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-
size:10pt;">35</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-
size:10pt;">&#32;percent in the </font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-
size:10pt;">second quarter</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-
size:10pt;">&#32;of 2016 when compared to the </font><font style="font-
family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">68</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-
size:10pt;">&#32;percent utilization achieved in the </font><font style="font-
family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">first</font><font style="font-
family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">&#32;quarter of </font><font style="font-
family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">2016</font><font style="font-
family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">. The decrease in marketed utilization in the 
</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">second 
quarter</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">&#32;of 2016 
reflects the reduced number of operating days in the </font><font style="font-
family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">second quarter</font><font style="font-
family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">&#32;as both the </font><font style="font-
family:inherit;font-size:10pt;font-style:italic;">Paragon MSS1</font><font 
style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">&#32;and </font><font style="font-
family:inherit;font-size:10pt;font-style:italic;">Paragon MSS2</font><font 
style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">&#32;completed contracts during the 
quarter</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;font-
style:italic;">.</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-
size:10pt;">&#32;Average daily revenues for Paragon&#8217;s floating rig fleet 
increased by </font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-
size:10pt;">51</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-
size:10pt;">&#32;percent to </font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-
size:10pt;">$399,000</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-
size:10pt;">&#32;per day in the </font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-
size:10pt;">second quarter</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-
size:10pt;">&#32;of </font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-
size:10pt;">2016</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-
size:10pt;">&#32;from </font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-
size:10pt;">$265,000</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-
size:10pt;">&#32;per rig in the </font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-
size:10pt;">first</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-
size:10pt;">&#32;quarter of </font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-
size:10pt;">2016</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">, 
reflecting that the </font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;font-
style:italic;">Paragon DPDS3</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-
size:10pt;">&#32;was the only floating rig under contract during the full 
quarter.  In addition, the company recognized revenue earned for unused shipyard
days upon completion of the </font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-
size:10pt;font-style:italic;">Paragon MSS2&#8217;s </font><font style="font-
family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">contract.</font></div><div style="line-
height:120%;padding-bottom:12px;text-align:justify;font-size:10pt;"><font

marketed jackup rig fleet was lower at </font><font style="font-

during the </font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">second 
quarter</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">.  Average daily
revenues for Paragon&#8217;s jackup fleet during the </font><font style="font-
family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">second quarter</font><font style="font-

height:120%;text-align:justify;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-
family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">At the end of the </font><font style="font-

family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">&#32;of </font><font style="font-
family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">2016</font><font style="font-
family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">, an estimated 29 percent of the company&#8217;s
marketed rig operating days were committed for 2016, including 10 percent and 30
percent for floating and jackup rig days, respectively.  The calculations for 
committed operating days exclude available days related to rigs that were 
stacked and not marketed during the quarter. </font></div><div style="line-
height:120%;padding-bottom:12px;padding-top:16px;text-align:justify;font-
size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;font-
weight:bold;">Outlook</font></div><div style="line-height:120%;text-
align:justify;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-
size:10pt;">&#8220;We expect continued volatility in commodity prices throughout
the remainder of 2016,&#8221; Mr. Stilley said.  &#8220;As we search for signs 
of increasing activity, we are nevertheless positioning the company for success 
by looking at innovative ways to maintain our position as the high quality, low 
cost offshore drilling contractor.  Of course, our main efforts are centered 
around achieving a positive outcome to our restructuring process which would 
leave us with a much improved balance sheet.  We expect that process will be 
completed in October.&#8221;</font></div><div style="line-height:120%;padding-
bottom:12px;padding-top:16px;text-align:justify;font-size:10pt;"><font 
style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;font-weight:bold;">Paragon Provides 
Fleet Status Report and Information on Going Concern Risk</font></div><div 
style="line-height:120%;text-align:justify;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-
family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">Paragon also announced today that it issued a 
report on drilling rig status and contract information as of August 8, 
2016.&#160; The report, titled &#8220;Fleet Status Report,&#8221; can be 
accessed on the company's website at www.paragonoffshore.com under the 
&#8220;Our Fleet&#8221; or &#8220;Investor Relations-Fleet Status Reports&#8221;
sections of the website.</font></div><div style="line-height:120%;text-
align:justify;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-
size:10pt;"><br></font></div><div style="line-height:120%;text-
align:justify;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-
size:10pt;">The accompanying consolidated financial statements have been 
prepared assuming that Paragon will continue as a going concern and contemplate 
the realization of assets and the satisfaction of liabilities in the normal 
course of business. The company&#8217;s ability to continue as a going concern 
is contingent upon the Bankruptcy Court&#8217;s approval of its plan of 
reorganization. This represents a material uncertainty related to events and 
conditions that may cause significant doubt on the company&#8217;s ability to 
continue as a going concern and, therefore, the company may be unable to realize
its assets and discharge its liabilities in the normal course of business.  
During the period that the company is operating as debtors-in-possession under 
Chapter 11, Paragon may sell or otherwise dispose of or liquidate assets or 
settle liabilities, subject to the approval of the Bankruptcy Court or as 
otherwise permitted in the ordinary course of business (and subject to 
restrictions in the company&#8217;s debt agreements), for amounts other than 
those reflected in the company&#8217;s consolidated financial statements.  
Investors are urged to review the contents of the company&#8217;s Form 10-Q 
including the discussions under &#8220;Risk Factors&#8221; when the document is 
filed.</font></div><div style="line-height:120%;padding-bottom:12px;padding-
top:16px;text-align:justify;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-
family:inherit;font-size:10pt;font-weight:bold;">About Paragon 
Offshore</font></div><div style="line-height:120%;padding-bottom:12px;text-
align:justify;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-
size:10pt;">Paragon is a global provider of offshore drilling rigs.  
Paragon&#8217;s operated fleet includes 34 jackups, including
two high specification heavy duty/harsh environment jackups, four drillships, 
and two semisubmersibles. Paragon&#8217;s primary business is contracting its 
rigs, related equipment and work crews to conduct oil and gas drilling and 
workover operations for its exploration and production customers on a dayrate 
basis around the world. Paragon&#8217;s principal executive offices are located 
in Houston, Texas. Paragon is a public limited company registered in England and
Wales with company number 08814042 and registered office at 20-22 Bedford Row, 
London, WC1R 4JS, England. Additional information is available at 
www.paragonoffshore.com.</font></div><div style="line-height:120%;padding-
bottom:12px;padding-top:24px;text-align:justify;font-size:10pt;"><font
